<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_603a7584-65e4-4911-8948-9b80e4997db0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText14452832144569484758" style="display:none">The men and women of the Otherworld – witches, werewolves, demons, vampires – live unseen among us. Only now a reckless killer has torn down the wall, trapping one very human woman in the supernatural crossfire.<br /><br />Robyn moved to LA after her husband died to try to put some distance between herself and the life they had together. And the challenges of her job as the PR consultant to a Paris Hilton wannabe are pretty distracting. But then her celebutante is gunned down in a night club, and Robyn is suddenly the prime suspect. The two people most determined to clear her are her old friend, the half-demon tabloid reporter Hope Adams, and a homicide detective with an uncanny affinity for the dead.<br /><br />Soon Robyn finds herself in the heart of a world she never even knew existed – and which she was safer knowing nothing about . . .</span>

<div id="review_1719274825" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1719274825" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1719274825?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553588545" href="/book/show/6237475-living-with-the-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=mad-scientists">mad-scientists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=shapeshifters">shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=magic-powers">magic-powers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1719274825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2294525104982702504">Definitely my least enjoyed of the series - it was actually kind of hard to keep reading.<br/><br/>Armstrong changed writing styles to third person and shifted points of view a lot. Every chapter changed, and short chapters they were. Not only that, but almost all the points of views were from new characters of the series that don't have impact beyond this book. Her technique made her writing style suffer. When she switched from an intimate point of view to a distant one, the writing technique simplified </span>
  <span id="freeText2294525104982702504" style="display:none">Definitely my least enjoyed of the series - it was actually kind of hard to keep reading.<br /><br />Armstrong changed writing styles to third person and shifted points of view a lot. Every chapter changed, and short chapters they were. Not only that, but almost all the points of views were from new characters of the series that don't have impact beyond this book. Her technique made her writing style suffer. When she switched from an intimate point of view to a distant one, the writing technique simplified and became a little awkward. It was pretty noticeable.<br /><br />While previous books would introduce new characters before they came into their own books, not so here. There were several brand new characters taking a major role and I didn't know nor care about them. Robyn is simple and rather boring. I didn't care about the new necromancer. Their developed relationship seemed force and just there because a new relationship was supposed to be, not because the chemistry makes sense.<br /><br />Hope and Karl were the best POV but again I'm not crazy about either of them. There's just something off-putting about Hope getting off on people getting hurt and Karl randomly robbing people of their valuables. <br /><br />The story is semi-clever and inventive enough but the way it's told and the characterization? Ugh. There are no series regulars besides mild mention. The Kumpania were intriguing and demented, but this plot is lightweight in comparison to others.<br /><br />Reading this one doesn't advance the story unless you care about Hope and Karl's development into not caring about the council at the end of the book. Can be skipped. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2294525104982702504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_67366882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67366882" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/67366882?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553588545" href="/book/show/6237475-living-with-the-dead">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Women of the Otherworld series</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67366882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5873912998850412027">I can't shrug off the feeling that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7581.Kelley_Armstrong' title='Kelley Armstrong' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kelley Armstrong</a>'s <i>Women of the Otherworld</i> books are shifting more and more from urban fantasy to just plain mystery. But maybe I am just too used to her world and it seems too real to me? I don't know. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2813124.Living_with_the_Dead__Women_of_the_Otherworld___9_' title='Living with the Dead (Women of the Otherworld, #9) by Kelley Armstrong' rel='nofollow noopener'>Living with the Dead</a> is another entertaining but ultimately forgettable addition to one of my favorite series. Let me sum it up.<br/><br/>The positive:<br/><br/>1) This book is just as page-turning as Armstrong's previous novels. Well-paced and never boring.<br/><br/>2) Kumpania - a commune </span>
  <span id="freeText5873912998850412027" style="display:none">I can't shrug off the feeling that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7581.Kelley_Armstrong" title="Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelley Armstrong</a>'s <i>Women of the Otherworld</i> books are shifting more and more from urban fantasy to just plain mystery. But maybe I am just too used to her world and it seems too real to me? I don't know. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2813124.Living_with_the_Dead__Women_of_the_Otherworld___9_" title="Living with the Dead (Women of the Otherworld, #9) by Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">Living with the Dead</a> is another entertaining but ultimately forgettable addition to one of my favorite series. Let me sum it up.<br /><br />The positive:<br /><br />1) This book is just as page-turning as Armstrong's previous novels. Well-paced and never boring.<br /><br />2) Kumpania - a commune of clairvoyants - is a fascinating and twisted place, a lot of freaky stuff goes on there. <br /><br />3) The ending seems to hint at a larger story arc to come, something big that will shake up the entire Otherworld. Has Armstrong been planting seeds throughout the series? I am intrigued.<br /><br />The negative:<br /><br />1) The format shifts from 1st person narrative in the other books to 3rd person from as many as 5(!) POVs, thus bringing a completely different tone to this story.<br /><br />2) No hot romance! <i>Women of the Otherworld</i> books have never been paranormal romances, but I do expect some flirting, some steamy hooking-up in these stories. The only romantic aspect in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2813124.Living_with_the_Dead__Women_of_the_Otherworld___9_" title="Living with the Dead (Women of the Otherworld, #9) by Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">Living with the Dead</a> comes from Hope and Karl and their relationship is not the one I enjoy - Hope continues being totally useless with her passive "power" and Karl is as overprotective as ever. Yawn.<br /><br />3) In the end, the main conflict turns out to be much ado about nothing. The event that jump-starts the mystery simply doesn't warrant the body count accumulated by the end of the book.<br /><br />I am reading the next book in the series though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5873912998850412027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13387398272573158089" style="display:none">This is definitely my least favorite of the series, though I never thought to stop reading and it had my attention ENOUGH.         rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2739595959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5151406212996627193">Oh boy, there is a tonne going on in this one! <br/><br/>I love this series, at first I was hesitant but actually they are all really good books. Mainly being the characters and the way that Armstrong makes everything comprehensive. <br/><br/>So, focusing on this one, we follow Hope and Robyn into the insane world of clairvoyants. At first I did not enjoy reading this. This one in the series is taken from the view of so many people. Lots of characters to adjust to, the only one familiar being Hope. I found it all t</span>
  <span id="freeText5151406212996627193" style="display:none">Oh boy, there is a tonne going on in this one! <br /><br />I love this series, at first I was hesitant but actually they are all really good books. Mainly being the characters and the way that Armstrong makes everything comprehensive. <br /><br />So, focusing on this one, we follow Hope and Robyn into the insane world of clairvoyants. At first I did not enjoy reading this. This one in the series is taken from the view of so many people. Lots of characters to adjust to, the only one familiar being Hope. I found it all too confusing, learning character traits and thought processes when you only have a page and a half between each one just got a bit tedious. The chapters are ridiculously short in this one, but you do get used to it. Just try not to get put off in the beginning. <br /><br />If you like action this one is perfect for you! If you thought the last few were on the tame side this one is packed! Action scenes, fights, gunshots, murders, chases, manipulation, even SWAT teams, this has it all! It is all in there, so action lovers this one is for you. <br /><br />The book does have a more softer, sentimental side also, so softies you will also enjoy. Hope as a character for me is interesting. Battling the demon inside with her conflicting thoughts makes good reading, and also the development between her and Karl. I am not sure if she does have another book centered around her as I think this one wraps things up for her but I am interested in where she does go onto. <br /><br />So 3 stars from me. It was good but not the best in the series. I'm interested to see who's up next in the series, they are getting so so good! I am thoroughly enjoying these books. I recommend for any of you fantasy lovers! Make sure you start at the beginning though! </span>
  <a data-text-id="5151406212996627193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4785432519098777476">Kelley Armstrong has always been one of my fave authors - Bitten, Canadian, Virals - she's just the best! I've yet to read a book by her that I didn't enjoy, and then I picked up Living with the Dead.<br/><br/>Robyn comes to LA (her husband has recently passed away), and she gets herself into a pickle. She's a PR consultant for a Paris Hilton like celebrity, and suddenly her employer is murdered. And then someone else is murdered. You'd think that's fine and dandy, right? Nope. Because she fled the scene </span>
  <span id="freeText4785432519098777476" style="display:none">Kelley Armstrong has always been one of my fave authors - Bitten, Canadian, Virals - she's just the best! I've yet to read a book by her that I didn't enjoy, and then I picked up Living with the Dead.<br /><br />Robyn comes to LA (her husband has recently passed away), and she gets herself into a pickle. She's a PR consultant for a Paris Hilton like celebrity, and suddenly her employer is murdered. And then someone else is murdered. You'd think that's fine and dandy, right? Nope. Because she fled the scene both times. Robyn works with Hope Adams (who we've seen before, if you've read this series) and this crime may get solved!<br /><br />To start off, the book isn't bad by any means. I am in love with Clayton and Elena, and Paige and Lucas, and Jaime and Jeremy. Those are my Otherworld couples! Especially the latter, seriously - super hot. I highly recommend their books! I never cared much for Hope and Karl, and I didn't really care for Robyn. I felt like I didn't have a real connection with them so I just didn't want to read it. I wanted to see my faves! That's the problem with these types of series when there's a large array of characters with their own books - we won't enjoy all of them.<br /><br />The story itself is super engaging and really fun to watch. Hope has such an interesting personality with her demon present, so she's a unique character to follow. I also thought the entire murder mystery was cool as well. Story wise, I think this book is amazing! It has Kelley's amazing writing and an awesome plot. This story had my attention the whole time and I devoured the book in a night. It is VERY VERY VERY good.<br /><br />This book is more action, thriller and mystery than romance. I miss the sexy romance of the other Women of the Otherworld books, but maybe Kelley is taking this series in a different direction. I'm very curious as to how this series is going to play out...<br /><br />Overall, this wasn't my favourite Women of the Otherworld book. I hope the next books pick up and I see more of my faves about! It's still a great book, but is more for thriller lovers than the fans of the romance in this series.<br /><br />Two out of five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4785432519098777476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69652601" />
    <a title="Mel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2295424-mel"><img alt="Mel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305638929p2/2295424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69652601?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel" href="/user/show/2295424-mel">Mel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780679314868" href="/book/show/2880072-living-with-the-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69652601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3500928959575045111">In this ninth book in Armstrong's Women of the Otherworld series the author brings us something different: the protagonist is a non-supernatural. <br/>Robyn Peltier is a PR consultant with no special powers or abilities what so ever, well… except maybe attracting bad luck. She does know how to pick her friends though, as Hope Adams and Karl Marsten come to her rescue when Robyn's problems evolve from bad to worse. <br/><br/>This is another solid read by Kelley Armstrong. It read like a suspense novel, packed w</span>
  <span id="freeText3500928959575045111" style="display:none">In this ninth book in Armstrong's Women of the Otherworld series the author brings us something different: the protagonist is a non-supernatural. <br />Robyn Peltier is a PR consultant with no special powers or abilities what so ever, well… except maybe attracting bad luck. She does know how to pick her friends though, as Hope Adams and Karl Marsten come to her rescue when Robyn's problems evolve from bad to worse. <br /><br />This is another solid read by Kelley Armstrong. It read like a suspense novel, packed with action and a high pace. Armstrong crafts the story wonderfully and she has made up an amazing world of supernatural groups, some with very disturbing rules and morals. <br /><br />In several reviews I've read that others find Robyn and Hope to be boring because of their limited powers. To me that isn't an issue. The struggle is even bigger for these heroines and they do deliver as they outsmart everyone and come up with good solutions. Also: they learn from their mistakes. <br /><br />Even though there was very little romance in this book, this book was about love and trust: losing it, finding it and being to able to let go. It had quite some touching moments as we get to see Robyn's dead husband in his desperate quest to help his wife and we see Hope worry about her capability to stand on her own two feet. <br /><br />This book introduces some interesting characters who we hopefully get to see in further books: the mercenary clairvoyant Rhyse and the wonderful Finn; the necromancer cop. <br /><br />My two favorite people of this book however were Adelle, the deliciously wicked bitch of an antagonist, and Karl Marsten. <br />Karl Marsten...<br />Karl. Marsten. <br />*Sigh.*<br />I want one. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3500928959575045111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2119552121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2119552121" />
    <a title="Jay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10633920-jay"><img alt="Jay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586708278p2/10633920.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2119552121?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jay" href="/user/show/10633920-jay">Jay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10633920-jay?shelf=awesome-secondary-characters">awesome-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10633920-jay?shelf=cliche-overload">cliche-overload</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10633920-jay?shelf=book-goes-downhill">book-goes-downhill</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10633920-jay?shelf=face-meet-palm">face-meet-palm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10633920-jay?shelf=wtf-ending">wtf-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10633920-jay?shelf=annoying-hero">annoying-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10633920-jay?shelf=heroine-i-want-to-punch">heroine-i-want-to-punch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10633920-jay?shelf=please-stop-whining">please-stop-whining</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10633920-jay?shelf=hated">hated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10633920-jay?shelf=burn-it">burn-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2119552121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9795908848973889088">I have never in my life been this disgusted by a heroine. <br/><br/>No wait, this is way past disgust. I am sickened and absolutely <b>repulsed</b> by her.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>First, a little background info for those who are unfamiliar with this series:</u>
</b><br/>Hope is a half demon. In this series, half demons are the offspring of a full demon and a human. A full demon has craving for "chaos" (the negative and/or violent motivations/thoughts/emotions/experiences of people), as well as a "superpower" like fire, telekinesis, teleportation</span>
  <span id="freeText9795908848973889088" style="display:none">I have never in my life been this disgusted by a heroine. <br><br>No wait, this is way past disgust. I am sickened and absolutely <b>repulsed</b> by her.<br><br><b>
  <u>First, a little background info for those who are unfamiliar with this series:</u>
</b><br>Hope is a half demon. In this series, half demons are the offspring of a full demon and a human. A full demon has craving for "chaos" (the negative and/or violent motivations/thoughts/emotions/experiences of people), as well as a "superpower" like fire, telekinesis, teleportation... etc. Half demons only inherit the <b>superpower</b> of their demon parent, so they could be your friendly neighbour, best friend or your favourite barista with an extra sprinkle of X-Men in them. <br><br>Based on this, Hope is an anomaly - instead of a cool superpower, she ended up with the chaos craves. But they're not just <b>craves</b>, she gets high on them as well as turned on, and the more she crosses path with evil, the more she wants it. She basically has visions of murders and treats it as porn, a memory which she then uses to <u>fuel her nightly activities with her boyfriend.</u><br><br>So imagine this. You've been kidnapped, raped and murdered by some psycho. Your soul is sort of floating around, waiting for someone to bring your murderer to justice. Suddenly, this random woman bumps into him and she has a vision of your entire ordeal, as well as evidence that could get him convicted. Maybe even dig up your decomposing body for a proper burial, you know, #JustGirlyThings. But instead of the eternal peace you're hoping for, <b>this chick keeps replaying your murder in her mind for the sole purpose of using the "thrill" to spice up her sex life. </b> <br><br>Now imagine she bumped into a paedophile. Or for your own sanity, don't.<br><br>After every vision (where she was sipping/lapping up/drinking/absorbing the chaos), her eyes would glaze over in ecstasy, or her face would be "twisted in euphoria/bliss". <b>HOW. FUCKING. SICK.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499706469ra/23259829.gif" width="400" height="280" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Getting high on horrible and heinous crimes, Hope came across as perverted and sexually deprived, something you'd expect from the villain of a murder mystery, not the main character who was adored by literally everyone she met. Maybe if she had a darker, stronger personality, then it would have worked better. I could get behind a kick-ass heroine trying to fight her nature and cleverly using it to her advantage until she made this ability her bitch. But the whole <i>Little Miss Sunshine</i>, head in the sand bullshit Hope was doing instead got on my fucking nerves. Her sole focus was her relationship with Karl instead of the 1000 actually serious problems around her. <br><br>Any other heroine in this series would have quarantined herself or at least supplied the police with anonymous tip-offs, while working her ass off to fix herself. Hope didn't, she was mildly uncomfortable with it all but not nearly as disturbed as she should've been. She relied on Karl (boyfriend) to "pull her back from the edge", which is actually just Karl shouting her name until she was able to snap out of her trance.<br><br>I hated this ability in Book #8 (where Hope was the main character) and I even abandoned the story at 50%. Moving on to Book #9, the blurb made it seem like it was Robyn's book - a little weird since every heroine has been introduced before taking the main stage in their own book and Robyn was a complete stranger to us, but I wanted to see what Kelley Armstrong's world would look like from the POV of a human for a change. To my absolute disappointment, I adored Robyn (+Finn) yet we ended up in Hope's head for the majority of the time. Hence my rant ^^^<br><br><br><b>DEEP BREATHS, JAY. DEEP BREATHS. </b><br><br><br>It's sad because I would have rated this book at least 4 stars if Robyn and Finn were its sole focus, their story was interesting and I wanted to see way more of them. <br><br>Kelley Armstrong is an excellent author but she really tanked it with Hope. I just hope (heh) I never have to see her again but we're nearing the end of the series and this book really hinted at <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[her playing quite a big role in the oncoming final shitstorm <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505586677ra/23938256.gif" width="400" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9795908848973889088" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

One assumption leads to a bad decision leads to another assumption lead to another bad decision, etc. That's basically what the entire book is--assumptions and reactions. With <i>terrible</i> consequences. That and a bad guy who is an incredible narcissist with borderline sociopathic tendencies. Adele definitely makes my Top 10 All-Time Most Hateful Villains. She's right up there with Iago. </span>

<div id="review_131572347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131572347" />
    <a title="Carmel (Rabid Reads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4561998-carmel-rabid-reads"><img alt="Carmel (Rabid Reads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396922701p2/4561998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131572347?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmel (Rabid Reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmel (Rabid Reads)" href="/user/show/4561998-carmel-rabid-reads">Carmel (Rabid Reads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780307358042" href="/book/show/6381724-living-with-the-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131572347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14773313462420658188"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://www.rabidreads.ca/2012/11/review-living-with-dead-by-kelley.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>This book is the least <i>Otherworld</i>-ly out of the bunch and, as a result, also the one that I only passably enjoyed. Kelley Armstrong switches up her tried and true format in <i>Living with the Dead</i> and that was a big mistake in my opinion. Instead of sticking with her enthralling first person point of views she opts for that of the third person and gives the lead role to a previously unknown, human character. This installment also focuses on clairvoyants which are not a breed</span>
  <span id="freeText14773313462420658188" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://www.rabidreads.ca/2012/11/review-living-with-dead-by-kelley.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>This book is the least <i>Otherworld</i>-ly out of the bunch and, as a result, also the one that I only passably enjoyed. Kelley Armstrong switches up her tried and true format in <i>Living with the Dead</i> and that was a big mistake in my opinion. Instead of sticking with her enthralling first person point of views she opts for that of the third person and gives the lead role to a previously unknown, human character. This installment also focuses on clairvoyants which are not a breed of supernaturals that readers have seen overly much up until this point and the story casts them in a pretty unfavourable light. I didn't particularly enjoy this book the first time around and I liked it even less upon the second read. I guess that after 9 novels even someone as talented as Kelley Armstrong can struggle with writing an amazing story.<br><br><i>Living with the Dead</i> is very, very dark and not in a good way. Adele, the main villain, is beyond nasty. She's a sociopath and a cold blooded killer. Clairvoyants' abilities are as much a curse as they are a gift because they pretty much have a 99.99% chance of eventually going insane. Definitely not good odds. I think that Adele has been a wackjob since birth; her upbringing and powers are contributing factors but there's just something inherently wrong with her. She doesn't just kill people; she toys with them and does things that are beyond twisted. Adele has sex with a mentally disabled boy in order to manipulate him into using his powers to her benefit and then gets pregnant and uses her baby to barter her way into a cabal. She then seduces his teenage brother in an attempt to hide her child's paternity. This is just one example of what lengths she's willing to go to; everything's just a means to an end to Adele. She's truly one of the most heinous characters that I've ever encountered which made this book very difficult to read. <br><br>I was confused as to why Robyn, a human PR rep, was cast as the lead character. There's been no mention of her up until this point and, correct me if I'm wrong, but I believe that this is her one and only appearance in this entire series. One of the reasons why I enjoy the <i>Women of the Otherworld</i> series so much is because it follows the same characters over a twelve year span. I've grown to love all of Armstrong's creations and have a vested interest in their well-being while as Robyn came out of left field only to never be heard from again. I didn't dislike her, she's a grieving widower trying to move on with her life and I felt sorry for her, but I just didn't understand why the heck she was in this novel to begin with. Finn's another new character who's introduced in this installment; at least he's a supernatural but he too all but disappears after this book. Other than Hope and Karl, the overall story, writing style and protagonists just didn't fit in the <i>Otherworld</i> universe. <br><br><i>Living with the Dead</i> wasn't what I expected and I'd even go so far as to say that I was disappointed with this book which is a first for me where Kelley Armstrong is concerned. The story did nothing to advance the overall plot line of this series, most of the characters are strangers and I was beyond disgusted by Adele. Reading this novel a second time actually made me like it even less; I'm glad that the other 12 installments are phenomenal because if this book would have been one of the earlier ones I might not have continued with this series. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380325771i/691073.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14773313462420658188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1801135366" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1801135366" />
    <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller"><img alt="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517553177p2/13396599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1801135366?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1801135366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14463402537995113533">Even though the magic of the series has evaporated, Living with the Dead was <i>just</i> entertaining enough to keep me reading to the end. But I now find myself contemplating abandoning the series. No Humans Involved (book #7) was a golden nugget in a series I thought had died, and the main reason I continued to this point, but now I have to weigh the risk of slogging through another novel like this against the possibility of striking gold again. I’ve been working on this series for so long, I just do</span>
  <span id="freeText14463402537995113533" style="display:none">Even though the magic of the series has evaporated, Living with the Dead was <i>just</i> entertaining enough to keep me reading to the end. But I now find myself contemplating abandoning the series. No Humans Involved (book #7) was a golden nugget in a series I thought had died, and the main reason I continued to this point, but now I have to weigh the risk of slogging through another novel like this against the possibility of striking gold again. I’ve been working on this series for so long, I just don’t think I have the patience.<br><br>Okay, the book wasn’t as <i>horrible</i> as I’m making it out to be. But when compared to other urban fantasies (and early books in this series), it doesn’t really hold a candle. It’s a little better when compared to paranormal romances, but not by much. And there wasn’t even a romance in this one! Which brings me to my next rant…<br><br>I craved at least a <i>little</i> romance in this book. After all, it’s one of the main reasons I got hooked on the series in the first place (my friend referred to it once saying “I want more of that hot werewolf sex.” Which I laughed at because I couldn’t disagree). Then to add insult to the lack of steamy scenes, the sexual encounters that <i>did</i> make an appearance were fucking weird. Weird like very uncomfortable and icky, not weird like kinky. It left me feeling like I could’ve been very happy living my life never having read about it. I’ll leave it at that.<br><br>Overall, the basic writing was still quality, the characters were good, the storyline was meh, and the romance was nonexistent. Part of me wants to see how everything converges at the end of the series, but at this point it might be a long while before I get there, if I do at all.<br><br>Recommendations: if you like urban fantasy, definitely check out the first two books – amazing! The rest of the series to this point has some merit, with a hit or miss ratio at about 50/50. This installment was my least favorite so far. I think I’m at the point where I’M the one who needs the recommendation on whether or not to finish out the series.<br><br>Via The Obsessive Bookseller at <a href="https://www.nikihawkes.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.NikiHawkes.com</a><br><br>Other books you might like:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/172764.Full_Moon_Rising__Riley_Jenson_Guardian__1_" title="Full Moon Rising (Riley Jenson Guardian #1) by Keri Arthur" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer6833373067612420994">I should say I really dislike the character of Hope in this series. It must say something good about Armstrong's talent for creating characters that I have this reaction. I can't stand Hope and that made it impossible for me to finish this book. Mostly because Hope is mentally worrying all the time about how she would react if Karl leaves her, instead of, say, how she would react if Karl got killed by a mutt. Which just goes to show what type of person Hope is. Honestly, maybe you, Hope dear, sh</span>
  <span id="freeText6833373067612420994" style="display:none">I should say I really dislike the character of Hope in this series. It must say something good about Armstrong's talent for creating characters that I have this reaction. I can't stand Hope and that made it impossible for me to finish this book. Mostly because Hope is mentally worrying all the time about how she would react if Karl leaves her, instead of, say, how she would react if Karl got killed by a mutt. Which just goes to show what type of person Hope is. Honestly, maybe you, Hope dear, should really worry about your friend.<br /><br />Additionally, the shifts in viewpoint are good in terms of breaking with the standard but too often the reader is told the same thing more than once by different characters. Still I made it over half way, and Armstrong's writing is a cut above much of the rest of slush pile that is UF these days. This book hasn't turned me off her, not by a long shot, but I just don't like Hope.</span>

<div id="review_32116765" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/32116765" />
    <a title="Julie (jjmachshev)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/882708-julie-jjmachshev"><img alt="Julie (jjmachshev)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208126390p2/882708.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/32116765?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie (jjmachshev)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie (jjmachshev)" href="/user/show/882708-julie-jjmachshev">Julie (jjmachshev)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/882708-julie-jjmachshev?shelf=2008-reads">2008-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32116765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13605695999641112135">Now how do I rate Kelley Armstrong's latest in her 'Women of the Otherworld' series? "Living with the Dead" isn't about just one woman. In a lot of ways it's not even about one couple, it's really about two men, two women, a ghost, and the question of what is love.<br/><br/>Robyn is a woman who recently lost her love, her soulmate, to a senseless and stupid crime. She spends her time now just going through the motions of living and keeping a scrapbook about good samaritans who are killed for their deeds, </span>
  <span id="freeText13605695999641112135" style="display:none">Now how do I rate Kelley Armstrong's latest in her 'Women of the Otherworld' series? "Living with the Dead" isn't about just one woman. In a lot of ways it's not even about one couple, it's really about two men, two women, a ghost, and the question of what is love.<br /><br />Robyn is a woman who recently lost her love, her soulmate, to a senseless and stupid crime. She spends her time now just going through the motions of living and keeping a scrapbook about good samaritans who are killed for their deeds, furthering reinforcing the futility and stupidity of her husband's death. When, through no real fault of her own, she becomes embroiled in a battle between two supernatural factions in LA, she ends up running for her life with no idea of why she's become a target.<br /><br />Hope is Robyn's best friend and she and her werewolf boyfriend Karl have come to LA to do a story, but really to check on Robyn. These two will have to use all their abilities (she's half demon) to keep Robyn alive long enough to figure out who's after her and why! Then we also have a cop necromancer thrown into the mix. And with Robyn's dead husband joining the search for Robyn and her pursuers, the mix is set. <br /><br />If you're looking for a pure romance, don't look here. If you're looking for a mystery with paranormal elements, an unusual love story that will make you ponder what love is and is not, a story about when and how grief affects different people, and a story about just how whacked out some fringe groups can get...then really pick up "Living With the Dead". You may not exactly be smiling at the end of the book, but you will be panting for the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13605695999641112135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_746290760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/746290760" />
    <a title="Beth The Vampire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22241496-beth-the-vampire"><img alt="Beth The Vampire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483516030p2/22241496.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/746290760?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth The Vampire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth The Vampire" href="/user/show/22241496-beth-the-vampire">Beth The Vampire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780356500232" href="/book/show/9826348-living-with-the-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=series-6-to-10">series-6-to-10</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=demons">demons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer746290760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3512701256852944209"><b>ACTUAL RATING 3.5</b><br/><br/>I’ve been grappling with this book overnight, trying to assess the story and the ending, trying to decide whether I liked it. And instead of my decision being black and white, it has turned out more a shade of grey.<br/><br/>Robyn, PR to a popular LA socialite, finds herself the main suspect in her clients murder. Chased by the police, and being followed by a mysterious young woman looking to harm her, Robyn does what any normal human person would do, and freaks out. Thankfully Robyn has </span>
  <span id="freeText3512701256852944209" style="display:none"><b>ACTUAL RATING 3.5</b><br /><br />I’ve been grappling with this book overnight, trying to assess the story and the ending, trying to decide whether I liked it. And instead of my decision being black and white, it has turned out more a shade of grey.<br /><br />Robyn, PR to a popular LA socialite, finds herself the main suspect in her clients murder. Chased by the police, and being followed by a mysterious young woman looking to harm her, Robyn does what any normal human person would do, and freaks out. Thankfully Robyn has two powerful friends, Hope (a half demon who can sense chaos), and her boyfriend Karl (a pack werewolf), who are able to untangle the web she has been caught in, and assist from a more supernatural point of view. The situation turns out to be a lot deeper than the death of Robyn’s employer, and involved the Nasts and Cabals, as well as a secret commune of clairvoyants. The detective in charge, who is able to speak to ghosts, is assigned the case, but the matter becomes more complicated when the ghost helping him just happens to be that of Robyn’s recently murdered husband.<br /><br />It’s not a bad story, it’s just….convoluted. There is no way this situation had to become this complicated. I feel that Hope and Karl actually made the whole situation about 10 times worse by becoming involved and trying to control everything. Then when it all came to a climax, it didn’t seem to wrap itself up. Robyn was still suspected of three murders, including one of a cop, and it just said the Cabals were going to bribe and divert all further attention until the matter just went away. I’m sorry, but no. How is the detective, Finn, supposed to explain all of it? Half a dozen people died on his case, there was an ambush involving a private tactical unit on the clairvoyant compound, and again a COP has been gunned down in the street, and all of this is just going to be pushed under the rug? In a story where there are numerous supernaturals, that part just goes beyond all belief.<br /><br />What I do love about this book, and what I have loved about all the previous entries into the series, is the characterisation. Hope is a really interesting young women, who is just coming to terms with her power and what that means. By the end she realises that she needs to make a decision by herself, even if it means sending Karl away, which she does. She does it for her, so she can make her own decisions without him making them on her behalf so she doesn’t have to make the hard choices, keeping her closeted and protected. It’s a great step forward for her, and I’m proud of her for that. Robyn was pretty throwaway for me, Karl was his usual….manish….self. Finn was the most interesting addition, but I didn’t get much of his backstory or even where his future is headed. I get the feeling that we won’t be seeing him again though.<br /><br />The first two books in the Women of the Otherworld series were excellent, with <i>Bitten</i> still being one of my favourites. The third book was a major downer that made me want to throw the paperback across the room, but then it started to pick up again, although never really meeting the same heights of the beginning. We’re in the tail end of the series now, and there were hints in <i>Living with the Dead</i> of something larger on the horizon. There have been a number of mysterious happenings in the supernatural world recently, and taken together they cannot mean anything good. I’m interested to see where it all ends up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3512701256852944209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_179041695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179041695" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/179041695?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=otherworld">otherworld</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179041695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3191717551071182426">This didn't feel like an Otherworld book. At all. It was deeply disturbing and dark. It featured some characters we know: primarily Hope and Karl, but unlike any of the previous books, this was written in the third person and the real main character was a regular human we've never met before.<br/><br/>It's been six months since Robyn's husband Damon died. Since then, she's moved to LA to start a new life for herself. She's a PR rep for a celebutante, but she's really just going through the motions. Hope i</span>
  <span id="freeText3191717551071182426" style="display:none">This didn't feel like an Otherworld book. At all. It was deeply disturbing and dark. It featured some characters we know: primarily Hope and Karl, but unlike any of the previous books, this was written in the third person and the real main character was a regular human we've never met before.<br /><br />It's been six months since Robyn's husband Damon died. Since then, she's moved to LA to start a new life for herself. She's a PR rep for a celebutante, but she's really just going through the motions. Hope is worried about her --the two are longtime friends-- so she and Karl come to visit. Shortly after they arrive, Robyn's client is killed and thanks to a string of unlikely events, Robyn becomes the prime suspect. Then Karl and Hope must figure out who really killed the woman and why, while protecting Robyn from the real killer.<br /><br />Investigating the case is Detective John Finnley. Finn's a necromancer, though he doesn't even really know what that means. He only knows that he occasionally sees ghosts... a skill that helps him believe Robyn is innocent, not only of her client's murder but other deaths that are piling up in her wake. The ghosts of the victims help lead his way, and so does (eventually) the ghost of Robyn's husband.<br /><br />Earlier, I mentioned that this story is disturbing. That's due almost entirely to our villain, a sociopathic clairvoyant named Adele. She is the real killer. It's not because she enjoys killing; she's just looking out for number one. You see, Robyn's client had the misfortune of accidentally taking an incriminating photo of Adele. That leads to her death. And the deaths that follow are also to keep Adele's secret -- that she is trying to escape from her commune of clairvoyants to join the Nast cabal. That doesn't sound that bad... standard bad-guy stuff. But there's more to her schemes. She slips birth control pills to one of her commune sisters, knowing it will eventually force the girl into what's essentially gang rape when she can't conceive a child by her husband. The husband Adele wanted for her own. She has sex with a mentally disabled boy to manipulate him into sharing his powers with her, and gets pregnant with his child. Then she seduces his younger brother, a 15 year-old, to hide the baby's paternity. She doesn't care what she has to do or who she has to do it to, to get what she wants.<br /><br />Adele is really a product of the environment she has grown up in... although undoubtedly, she is the worst case scenario. The commune beats its children to instill fear of the cabals; it inbreeds; uses the disabled for their powers; and we've already talked about the forced sex. It even kills those whose powers are too weak to make them useful. And even as I try to describe all this, I know it doesn't do it justice.<br /><br />There's a lot going on here. In addition to all the stuff with Robyn, Finn &amp; Adele, we can't forget about Hope and Karl. Their relationship is at a crossroads. And Hope has a lot of uncertainty about her future. And in the end, we see that the major developments in this book and the previous ones are intertwined, perhaps in some greater purpose, or bigger picture. I find that very intriguing. It was a solid installment... it just felt... off. And I missed the romance. 4 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3191717551071182426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_74057880" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74057880" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1325398-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272546019p2/1325398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74057880?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/1325398-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1325398-jennifer?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74057880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14333406696465389550">This review was originally posted on my review blog : Falling Off The Shelf.<br/><br/>Robyn Peltier never knew that moving to Los Angelas would be such a eye-opening experience. It's one thing following around a famous celebutante like Portia Kane, clearly another when your being chased down by psychotic murderers. All she ever wanted to do was move away from the horrible memories of her husbands death, not walk straight into more. When her client is gunned down in the back room of a local night club, Rob</span>
  <span id="freeText14333406696465389550" style="display:none">This review was originally posted on my review blog : Falling Off The Shelf.<br /><br />Robyn Peltier never knew that moving to Los Angelas would be such a eye-opening experience. It's one thing following around a famous celebutante like Portia Kane, clearly another when your being chased down by psychotic murderers. All she ever wanted to do was move away from the horrible memories of her husbands death, not walk straight into more. When her client is gunned down in the back room of a local night club, Robyn is the prime suspect for murder. <br /><br />Hope Adams is Robyn's best friend, and she will do anything to clear her good friend's name. It's crazy enough that Robyn is being hunted down by the police for a murder she didn't commit, but now they have to worry about being stuck in the middle of a turf war between Otherworld Cabals. Hope wants to keep the secrets of the Otherworld as far from her friend's ears as possible, but it may be the only way to save her. It's going to take a lot of help to clear her of this one, and Hope knows just the people who can get the job done.<br /><br />I've been a big fan of Kelley Armstrong's Women of the Otherworld Series, and it's no surprise that I would love this book. I read a lot of reviews on Amazon before reading this book, and I was a bit skeptical. A lot of people said they got confused with the constant point-of-view change, but personally I didn't have a problem with it at all. Don't get me wrong, there were a lot of different point-of-views in this installment, from Robyn, to Hope, to Karl, and even the murderer. It was a real brain boggler in the beginning. As soon as I got my bearings, which didn't take long, just a few short chapters, I was able to enjoy this book as much as I have enjoyed every other installment in this fabulous series.<br /><br />I loved how Robyn was determined to do her part in helping to find the murderer of her client, while not really knowing the full scheme of things. She put herself in danger quite a few times, and on many occasions needed the help of her friends to get out of it, but she did it in stride. I honestly don't know how I would react in her situation, being hunted by both the police and a psychotic killer. I'd probably end up climbing under my bed and hoping for the best.<br /><br />I was super excited to finally learn more about Hope Adams, and her lover Karl Marsten. They've shown their faces in previous installments in this series, but I've been wondering when they would surface as main characters. They had always had an on and off again romance brewing, and it was nice to see how things turned out between them here. <br /><br />I'm worried about what will occur in the coming novels with Hope though, because she has some big choices to make, and I hope she will make the right ones. It makes me want to pick up the next installment right now and read it, but unfortunately I'll have to find a way to get my hands on it first. I can't wait to see where things will go with the Otherworld in the next installment, Frostbitten.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14333406696465389550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_254830335" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/254830335" />
    <a title="Celine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3387843-celine"><img alt="Celine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460292659p2/3387843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/254830335?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celine" href="/user/show/3387843-celine">Celine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=werewolves-shifters">werewolves-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254830335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15624823093993129170">In <i>Living with the Dead</i> we continue with the Hope and Karl storyline, this time adding Hope's best friend Robyn. On many points <i>Living with the Dead</i> is very different from its eight predecessors, and in my opinion this is not a good thing. <br/><br/>After being widowed at twenty-eight, Robyn takes the job of being Portia's PR person. When Portia is murdered in a club and Robyn flights the scene to chase after the killer, she is number one suspect on the police's list. Together with her friend Hope and Hop</span>
  <span id="freeText15624823093993129170" style="display:none">In <i>Living with the Dead</i> we continue with the Hope and Karl storyline, this time adding Hope's best friend Robyn. On many points <i>Living with the Dead</i> is very different from its eight predecessors, and in my opinion this is not a good thing. <br /><br />After being widowed at twenty-eight, Robyn takes the job of being Portia's PR person. When Portia is murdered in a club and Robyn flights the scene to chase after the killer, she is number one suspect on the police's list. Together with her friend Hope and Hope's boyfriend Karl, she gets caught up in several plots to kill her.<br /><br />Overall I think <i>Living with the Dead</i>'s main problem is the severe lack of focus. The story is all over the place, with tons of characters each having their own motivation for their actions. <i>Living with the Dead</i> is written from multiple points of view in third person, creating a whole chorus of voices instead of the steady, personal first person view we're used to.<br /><br />One of Ms Armstrong's forte's is usually creating a mystery. I'm always fully engaged into the plot, trying to figure everything out along with the characters. Because we have so many POVs here, the reader is privy to more information than the characters. For example, the reader knows Detective Finn is actually a good guy trying to help, while Robyn and Hope are constantly trying to stay away from him. I absolutely hate having to see characters making prejudices about each other while all I want to do is bump their heads together and scream "YOU'RE ON THE SAME SIDE HERE!". This all makes for a frustrating, and in the end unsatisfying read.<br /><br />It saddened me to see Hope and Karl's relationship to be reduced to a standard male-dominated one. I don't think Hope stood her ground enough, and most of the story she felt more like a needy puppy than an adult woman. I love the couples in the Women of the Otherworld series that are equals, like Paige and Lucas. Hope and Karl were okay in the previous book, <i>Personal Demon</i>, but I don't think <i>Living with the Dead</i> did them justice. In <i>Personal Demon</i> I loved how they were sweet to each other, how they had a healthy and loving relationship&gt;. I didn't see any of that in <i>Living with the Dead</i>. There are no romantic moments, most of the time it's just Karl ordering Hope around. <br /><br />In the end I did enjoy the story, even though at times it is overly gruesome (it features a commune that celebrates inbreeding and torture of children). Ms Armstrong knows how to write an engaging story. Sadly <i>Living with the Dead</i> was my least favourite book of her so far.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15624823093993129170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1916428303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1916428303" />
    <a title="Alyssa Nelson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4665768-alyssa-nelson"><img alt="Alyssa Nelson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397027844p2/4665768.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1916428303?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa Nelson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa Nelson" href="/user/show/4665768-alyssa-nelson">Alyssa Nelson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665768-alyssa-nelson?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665768-alyssa-nelson?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665768-alyssa-nelson?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665768-alyssa-nelson?shelf=canadian-author">canadian-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1916428303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9718852306168683615">This was the weakest book of this series that I’ve read so far. My guess is that it’s because it’s mainly told from the perspectives of people who don’t know about the supernatural community, but that information has to be present somehow; I also felt as though the story itself dragged. I was about a quarter of the way in when I thought: wow, that’s short, it’s going to end soon! And then I kept having that same thought the rest of the way through.<br/><br/>It’s not a bad book, however, it’s just that the</span>
  <span id="freeText9718852306168683615" style="display:none">This was the weakest book of this series that I’ve read so far. My guess is that it’s because it’s mainly told from the perspectives of people who don’t know about the supernatural community, but that information has to be present somehow; I also felt as though the story itself dragged. I was about a quarter of the way in when I thought: wow, that’s short, it’s going to end soon! And then I kept having that same thought the rest of the way through.<br /><br />It’s not a bad book, however, it’s just that the other books of the series are amazing, so this pretty good one fell flat. It follows typical Women of the Otherworld style, where it has a little bit of romance going on, but that’s a side note to the main thriller aspect of the book. The antagonist of this book is truly crazy, which led to a lot of intense, very sad situations. I like that we get to see a couple of outsiders being brought into the fold and see what it’s like when they realize that the world isn’t as straightforward as they thought it was. My favorite part was all of the misunderstandings that arise when the characters tried the theorize as to what was going on — everyone kept overthinking the series of events and were so mistrustful of everyone else so that it took a really long time for the characters to work out who was actually on whose side and who they could work with.<br /><br />I liked reading about more of Hope and Karl, and it was nice to see Hope taking charge. Their relationship is develops a bit more in this series, but what’s important is that Hope is starting to figure out who she is and what she wants, so in order to make room for that, their relationship is left dangling at the end, so I’m hoping to get some resolution on that in the next book.<br /><br />Basically, this is an amazing series, and this was a pretty-okay installment of it. I’m hoping this book was just a hiccup for the series overall and it doesn’t signal a decline to one of my favorite all-time series, but I’ll have to read the others to find out!<br /><br />Also posted on <a href="http://www.purplereaders.com/?p=3826" rel="nofollow noopener">Purple People Readers</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9718852306168683615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_74572274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74572274" />
    <a title="Melindeeloo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2766907-melindeeloo"><img alt="Melindeeloo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1266031818p2/2766907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74572274?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melindeeloo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melindeeloo" href="/user/show/2766907-melindeeloo">Melindeeloo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>
